# Task: Design a Priority-Based Shard Allocation Strategy

## Background
Elasticsearch's shard allocation balances shards across nodes, but doesn't support priority-based allocation where critical indices get preferred placement on faster nodes.

## Objective
Design a new `PriorityShardsAllocator` that extends the existing allocation framework to support index-priority-aware shard placement.

## Steps
1. Study the existing shard allocation in `server/src/main/java/org/elasticsearch/cluster/routing/allocation/`
2. Understand the `ShardsAllocator` interface and `BalancedShardsAllocator`
3. Study `AllocationDeciders` and how decisions compose
4. Create a design document `design_doc.md` in `/workspace/` with:
   - Architecture overview of current allocation
   - Proposed PriorityShardsAllocator class design
   - New `AllocationDecider` for priority constraints
   - Index setting for priority level (`index.routing.allocation.priority`)
   - Interaction with existing deciders (DiskThresholdDecider, AwarenessAllocationDecider)
   - API changes needed
5. Create a skeleton Java file `PriorityShardsAllocator.java` showing the class structure

## Key Reference Files
- `server/src/main/java/org/elasticsearch/cluster/routing/allocation/allocator/BalancedShardsAllocator.java`
- `server/src/main/java/org/elasticsearch/cluster/routing/allocation/allocator/ShardsAllocator.java`
- `server/src/main/java/org/elasticsearch/cluster/routing/allocation/decider/AllocationDeciders.java`

## Success Criteria
- Design doc exists with architecture overview
- Skeleton Java file exists
- Design references existing allocation classes
- Includes interaction with existing deciders

642026-03-11T04:33:39.288487agentmessage-
I am thinking...: Now I have a thorough understanding of the codebase. Let me plan the two deliverables:

## 1. design_doc.md

The design document needs to cover:
- Architecture overview
- Proposed PriorityShardsAllocator design
- New AllocationDecider for priority constraints
- Index setting `index.routing.allocation.priority`
- Interaction with existing deciders

Key facts from the codebase:
- `ShardsAllocator` interface: `allocate(RoutingAllocation)`, `decideShardAllocation(ShardRouting, RoutingAllocation)`
- `BalancedShardsAllocator` is the main implementation - uses WeightFunction with theta0-theta3 for shard/index/writeLoad/diskUsage balance
- `AllocationDecider` base class with `canAllocate`, `canRemain`, `canRebalance`, etc.
- `AllocationDeciders` aggregates all deciders - returns NO immediately on first NO (in non-debug mode)
- `PriorityComparator` already exists in `org.elasticsearch.gateway` - orders shards by: system > priority (desc) > creation_date (desc) > name
- `IndexMetadata.SETTING_PRIORITY` = "index.priority" and `INDEX_PRIORITY_SETTING` already exists
- `AllocationPriorityTests.java` tests existing priority-based allocation ordering

The new setting `index.routing.allocation.priority` is DIFFERENT from the existing `index.priority`. The existing `index.priority` controls the ORDER in which unassigned shards are recovered (via PriorityComparator). The new `index.routing.allocation.priority` would control WHERE shards are allocated (which nodes they prefer).

[Existing Priority Mechanisms](#2-existing-priority-mechanisms)\n3. [New Index Setting: `index.routing.allocation.priority`](#3-new-index-setting-indexroutingallocationpriority)\n4. [Operational Considerations](#8-operational-considerations)\n\n---\n\n## 1. Architecture Overview\n\n### 1.1 Elasticsearch Allocation Pipeline\n\nShard allocation in Elasticsearch is orchestrated by `AllocationService`, which coordinates two distinct subsystems:\n\n```\nClusterState change\n       \u2502\n       \u25bc\n AllocationService.reroute()\n       \u2502\n       \u251c\u2500\u25ba ExistingShardsAllocator (GatewayAllocator)\n       \u2502       Recovers shards from existing node-local copies\n       \u2502\n       \u2514\u2500\u25ba ShardsAllocator  \u25c4\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500 focus of this design\n               \u2502\n               \u251c\u2500\u25ba allocateUnassigned()   \u2014 place unassigned shards\n               \u251c\u2500\u25ba moveShards()           \u2014 evict shards that violate constraints\n               \u2514\u2500\u25ba balance()             \u2014 rebalance for even distribution\n```\n\nEvery candidate node assignment produced by `ShardsAllocator` is gated through `AllocationDeciders`, an ordered chain of `AllocationDecider` implementations. A single `NO` verdict from any decider blocks the placement.\n\n### 1.2 Current Allocator Implementations\n\n| Class | Strategy |\n|---|---|\n| `BalancedShardsAllocator` | Weight-function balancing across shard count, index spread, write load, and disk usage |\n| `DesiredBalanceShardsAllocator` | Async desired-balance computation delegating to `BalancedShardsAllocator` |\n\n### 1.3 Where PriorityShardsAllocator Fits\n\n`PriorityShardsAllocator` is a new `ShardsAllocator` implementation that wraps `BalancedShardsAllocator` as a delegate. It intercepts the unassigned-shard queue before the delegate sees it, reorders shards by their allocation priority tier, and then lets the delegate perform its normal weight-based placement within each tier.\n\n```\nAllocationService\n       \u2502\n       \u2514\u2500\u25ba PriorityShardsAllocator          (new)\n                   \u2502\n                   \u251c\u2500 sort unassigned shards by index.routing.allocation.priority (desc)\n                   \u2502\n                   \u2514\u2500\u25ba BalancedShardsAllocator (delegate)\n                               \u2502\n                               \u2514\u2500\u25ba AllocationDeciders\n                                       \u251c\u2500 PriorityAllocationDecider  (new)\n                                       \u251c\u2500 DiskThresholdDecider\n                                       \u251c\u2500 FilterAllocationDecider\n                                       \u251c\u2500 ShardsLimitAllocationDecider\n                                       \u251c\u2500 ThrottlingAllocationDecider\n                                       \u2514\u2500 \u2026 (all other existing deciders)\n```\n\n---\n\n## 2. Existing Priority Mechanisms\n\nUnderstanding the existing priority infrastructure is essential to avoid duplication and ensure the new design integrates cleanly.\n\n### 2.1 `index.priority` (Recovery Ordering)\n\n**Setting:** `IndexMetadata.INDEX_PRIORITY_SETTING` (`index.priority`, integer \u2265 0, default `1`)\n\n**Purpose:** Controls the order in which unassigned shards are handed to the recovery pipeline. Higher values are recovered first.\n\n**Implementation:** `PriorityComparator` (in `org.elasticsearch.gateway`) sorts `ShardRouting` instances by:\n1. System indices first\n2. `index.priority` descending\n3. `index.creation_date` descending (newer indices first)\n4. Index name descending (lexicographic tiebreak)\n\n**Scope:** Recovery ordering only \u2014 it does not influence *which node* a shard lands on.\n\n### 2.2 `AllocationPriorityTests`\n\nThe existing test `AllocationPriorityTests.testPrioritizedIndicesAllocatedFirst` validates that `index.priority` causes high-priority index shards to enter the `INITIALIZING` state before low-priority ones when throttled by `ThrottlingAllocationDecider`. This test exercises the existing mechanism and is unaffected by the new design.\n\n### 2.3 Gap Addressed by This Design\n\n`index.priority` answers *when* a shard is recovered. It does not answer:\n- *Which nodes* are preferred or reserved for high-priority indices.\n- How to prevent low-priority index shards from consuming node capacity that high-priority shards need.\n- How to express a multi-tier priority model independently of recovery ordering.\n\nThe new `index.routing.allocation.priority` setting and its associated allocator/decider fill this gap.\n\n---\n\n## 3. New Index Setting: `index.routing.allocation.priority`\n\n### 3.1 Definition\n\n```\nSetting key:  index.routing.allocation.priority\nType:         integer\nScope:        IndexScope\nDefault:      1\nValid range:  1 \u2013 10  (inclusive)\nDynamic:      yes (changeable via Index Settings API without restart)\n```\n\n**Semantics:** A higher value means the index's shards are allocated before lower-valued indices when node capacity is constrained, and that nodes tagged with a minimum priority attribute will accept the index's shards.\n\n### 3.2 Priority Tiers\n\n| Value | Suggested Use |\n|---|---|\n| 10 | Mission-critical system indices, SLA-bound write indices |\n| 7\u20139 | High-importance operational indices |\n| 4\u20136 | Standard production indices (default band) |\n| 2\u20133 | Background / analytics indices |\n| 1 | Best-effort, archival, or low-importance indices (default) |\n\n### 3.3 Relationship to `index.priority`\n\nThese two settings are orthogonal and serve different purposes:\n\n| Setting | Controls | Mechanism |\n|---|---|---|\n| `index.priority` | Recovery order (when) | `PriorityComparator` in `GatewayAllocator` |\n| `index.routing.allocation.priority` | Allocation preference (where, in what order) | `PriorityShardsAllocator` + `PriorityAllocationDecider` |\n\nAn index may have `index.priority = 100` (recover first) and `index.routing.allocation.priority = 1` (no node preference), or any other combination.\n\n### 3.4 Node Attribute: `node.attr.allocation.priority`\n\nTo enable node-level reservation, data nodes may be tagged with:\n\n```yaml\n# elasticsearch.yml on a dedicated high-priority node\nnode.attr.allocation.priority: 7\n```\n\nA node tagged with `node.attr.allocation.priority: N` will only accept shards from indices whose `index.routing.allocation.priority >= N`. This is enforced by `PriorityAllocationDecider`. Nodes without this attribute accept shards from any index regardless of priority.\n\n---\n\n## 4. PriorityShardsAllocator Design\n\n### 4.1 Class Structure\n\n```\norg.elasticsearch.cluster.routing.allocation.allocator\n\u2514\u2500\u2500 PriorityShardsAllocator   implements ShardsAllocator\n        \u2502\n        \u251c\u2500\u2500 INDEX_ROUTING_ALLOCATION_PRIORITY_SETTING  (Setting<Integer>)\n        \u251c\u2500\u2500 delegate: ShardsAllocator                  (BalancedShardsAllocator)\n        \u2502\n        \u251c\u2500\u2500 allocate(RoutingAllocation)\n        \u2502       \u2514\u2500\u2500 allocateByPriorityTiers(allocation)\n        \u2502               \u251c\u2500\u2500 groupUnassignedByPriority(routingNodes)  \u2192 SortedMap<Integer, List<ShardRouting>>\n        \u2502               \u251c\u2500\u2500 for each tier (high \u2192 low):\n        \u2502               \u2502       injectTierIntoUnassignedQueue(allocation, tierShards)\n        \u2502               \u2502       delegate.allocate(allocation)\n        \u2502               \u2514\u2500\u2500 delegate.allocate(allocation)  // moveShards + balance pass\n        \u2502\n        \u2514\u2500\u2500 decideShardAllocation(ShardRouting, RoutingAllocation)\n                \u2514\u2500\u2500 delegate.decideShardAllocation(shard, allocation)\n```\n\n### 4.2 Allocation Algorithm\n\n#### Phase 1 \u2014 Priority-Ordered Unassigned Allocation\n\n```\n1. Collect all UNASSIGNED shards from RoutingNodes.unassigned()\n2. Group shards by their index's index.routing.allocation.priority value\n3. Sort groups in descending priority order (10 first, 1 last)\n4. For each priority group (highest to lowest):\n     a. Present only this group's shards as the unassigned queue\n     b. Invoke delegate.allocateUnassigned()\n        \u2192 BalancedShardsAllocator places shards using its weight function\n        \u2192 AllocationDeciders (including PriorityAllocationDecider) gate each placement\n     c. Any shards the delegate could not place remain UNASSIGNED\n5. After all groups are processed, run delegate.moveShards() and delegate.balance()\n   on the full routing table (priority-agnostic rebalancing pass)\n```\n\nThis ensures that when node capacity is limited (e.g., throttled by `ThrottlingAllocationDecider`), available slots are consumed by the highest-priority shards first.\n\n#### Phase 2 \u2014 Move and Balance Pass\n\nAfter priority-ordered initial placement, the standard move and balance passes run without priority filtering. This preserves the cluster's long-term balance properties and ensures shards that violate constraints (e.g., disk watermarks) are relocated regardless of priority.\n\n### 4.3 `decideShardAllocation` (Explain API)\n\nThe explain API path delegates directly to `BalancedShardsAllocator.decideShardAllocation`. Priority ordering is a queue-level concern and does not change the per-node allocation decision logic, so no wrapping is needed here.\n\n### 4.4 Settings Registration\n\n`INDEX_ROUTING_ALLOCATION_PRIORITY_SETTING` must be registered in `IndexScopedSettings` alongside the other `index.routing.allocation.*` settings. It is a dynamic, index-scoped integer setting.\n\n### 4.5 Guice / Module Wiring\n\n`PriorityShardsAllocator` is injected as the `ShardsAllocator` binding in `ClusterModule`, replacing or wrapping the existing binding. The `BalancedShardsAllocator` (or `DesiredBalanceShardsAllocator`) is injected as the delegate via constructor injection.\n\n```java\n// In ClusterModule (sketch)\nbind(ShardsAllocator.class).to(PriorityShardsAllocator.class);\n```\n\n---\n\n## 5. PriorityAllocationDecider Design\n\n### 5.1 Purpose\n\n`PriorityAllocationDecider` enforces node-level priority constraints. It prevents shards from indices with a low `index.routing.allocation.priority` from being placed on nodes that have been designated for high-priority workloads via `node.attr.allocation.priority`.\n\n### 5.2 Class Structure\n\n```\norg.elasticsearch.cluster.routing.allocation.decider\n\u2514\u2500\u2500 PriorityAllocationDecider   extends AllocationDecider\n        \u2502\n        \u251c\u2500\u2500 NAME = \"priority\"\n        \u2502\n        \u251c\u2500\u2500 canAllocate(ShardRouting, RoutingNode, RoutingAllocation) \u2192 Decision\n        \u2502       1. Read index priority from IndexMetadata\n        \u2502       2. Read node's allocation.priority attribute (if present)\n        \u2502       3. If node has no attribute \u2192 Decision.YES (unrestricted node)\n        \u2502       4. If index priority >= node minimum priority \u2192 Decision.YES\n        \u2502       5. Else \u2192 Decision.NO with explanation\n        \u2502\n        \u2514\u2500\u2500 canRemain(IndexMetadata, ShardRouting, RoutingNode, RoutingAllocation) \u2192 Decision\n                Same logic as canAllocate \u2014 ensures shards are evicted if node\n                priority attribute is raised above the index's priority.\n```\n\n### 5.3 Decision Logic\n\n```\nnodePriorityAttr = node.getAttributes().get(\"allocation.priority\")\n\nif nodePriorityAttr == null:\n    return Decision.YES   // node has no priority restriction\n\nnodeMinPriority = parseInt(nodePriorityAttr)\nindexPriority   = INDEX_ROUTING_ALLOCATION_PRIORITY_SETTING.get(indexMetadata.getSettings())\n\nif indexPriority >= nodeMinPriority:\n    return Decision.YES   // index meets or exceeds node's minimum priority\nelse:\n    return Decision.NO    // index priority too low for this node\n```\n\n### 5.4 `canRemain` Behavior\n\nWhen a node's `node.attr.allocation.priority` is raised (e.g., via a rolling restart), shards from indices whose priority falls below the new threshold will receive a `NO` from `canRemain`. `AllocationService` will then relocate those shards to nodes that accept them. This provides a clean mechanism for progressively dedicating nodes to higher-priority workloads.\n\n### 5.5 Registration\n\n`PriorityAllocationDecider` is added to the `ClusterModule.createAllocationDeciders()` list. Because `AllocationDeciders` short-circuits on the first `NO` in non-debug mode, the position of `PriorityAllocationDecider` in the list matters:\n\n- **Recommended position:** After `FilterAllocationDecider` and before `ThrottlingAllocationDecider`. This ensures hard filter constraints (require/include/exclude) are checked first, and throttling is applied only to placements that pass the priority gate.\n\n---\n\n## 6. Interaction with Existing Deciders\n\n### 6.1 Decider Evaluation Order (Non-Debug Mode)\n\n`AllocationDeciders.withDeciders()` iterates deciders in registration order and returns the first `NO` immediately. The full chain for a candidate placement is:\n\n```\n1.  ReplicaAfterPrimaryActiveAllocationDecider   \u2014 replica only after primary is active\n2.  RebalanceOnlyWhenActiveAllocationDecider     \u2014 rebalance only when all shards active\n3.  ClusterRebalanceAllocationDecider            \u2014 cluster-wide rebalance gate\n4.  ConcurrentRebalanceAllocationDecider         \u2014 concurrent rebalance throttle\n5.  EnableAllocationDecider                      \u2014 allocation enabled/disabled flag\n6.  NodeVersionAllocationDecider                 \u2014 version compatibility\n7.  SnapshotInProgressAllocationDecider          \u2014 snapshot safety\n8.  RestoreInProgressAllocationDecider           \u2014 restore safety\n9.  FilterAllocationDecider                      \u2014 require/include/exclude filters\n10. SameShardAllocationDecider                   \u2014 no two copies on same node\n11. DiskThresholdDecider                         \u2014 disk watermark enforcement\n12. ShardsLimitAllocationDecider                 \u2014 per-index and cluster shard limits\n13. AwarenessAllocationDecider                   \u2014 zone/rack awareness\n14. **PriorityAllocationDecider**  (NEW)         \u2014 node priority attribute gate\n15. ThrottlingAllocationDecider                  \u2014 concurrent recovery throttle\n16. MaxRetryAllocationDecider                    \u2014 max retry limit\n17. NodeShutdownAllocationDecider                \u2014 node shutdown awareness\n18. NodeReplacementAllocationDecider             \u2014 node replacement awareness\n```\n\n### 6.2 Interaction Details\n\n#### With `FilterAllocationDecider`\n\n`FilterAllocationDecider` enforces `index.routing.allocation.require/include/exclude` settings. `PriorityAllocationDecider` enforces `index.routing.allocation.priority` against `node.attr.allocation.priority`. These are independent constraints in the same namespace; both must pass for a placement to proceed.\n\n**Example:** An index with `index.routing.allocation.require._tier: data_hot` and `index.routing.allocation.priority: 8` must land on a hot-tier node that also has `node.attr.allocation.priority <= 8`.\n\n#### With `ThrottlingAllocationDecider`\n\n`ThrottlingAllocationDecider` limits concurrent recoveries per node. Because `PriorityShardsAllocator` presents high-priority shards first, throttle slots are consumed by high-priority shards before low-priority ones even get to the throttle check. This is the primary mechanism by which priority ordering translates into preferential resource consumption.\n\n#### With `DiskThresholdDecider`\n\nDisk constraints are absolute and take precedence over priority. A high-priority shard cannot be placed on a node that has exceeded the high watermark. The priority ordering in `PriorityShardsAllocator` ensures that when disk space is available, it is allocated to high-priority shards first.\n\n#### With `ShardsLimitAllocationDecider`\n\nPer-node shard limits apply uniformly regardless of priority. If a node is at its `index.routing.allocation.total_shards_per_node` limit, no shard \u2014 regardless of priority \u2014 can be placed there.\n\n#### With `AwarenessAllocationDecider`\n\nZone/rack awareness constraints are orthogonal to priority. A high-priority shard still cannot violate awareness constraints. Priority ordering only affects which shards are attempted first within the set of constraint-satisfying placements.\n\n#### With `DesiredBalanceShardsAllocator`\n\nIf `DesiredBalanceShardsAllocator` is the active allocator (the default in recent Elasticsearch versions), `PriorityShardsAllocator` wraps it as the delegate instead of `BalancedShardsAllocator` directly. The desired-balance computation loop in `DesiredBalanceComputer` would need to be made priority-aware by sorting its internal unassigned shard iteration. This is a future enhancement; the initial implementation targets `BalancedShardsAllocator` as the delegate.\n\n---\n\n## 7. Configuration Reference\n\n### 7.1 Index Settings\n\n| Setting | Type | Default | Dynamic | Description |\n|---|---|---|---|---|\n| `index.routing.allocation.priority` | integer (1\u201310) | `1` | yes | Allocation priority tier for this index's shards |\n\n### 7.2 Node Attributes\n\n| Attribute | Type | Default | Description |\n|---|---|---|---|\n| `node.attr.allocation.priority` | integer (1\u201310) | *(absent)* | Minimum index priority this node will accept. Absent = unrestricted |\n\n### 7.3 Example Configurations\n\n**Designate a node for high-priority indices only:**\n```yaml\n# elasticsearch.yml\nnode.attr.allocation.priority: 7\n```\n\n**Mark an index as high-priority:**\n```json\nPUT /my-critical-index/_settings\n{\n  \"index.routing.allocation.priority\": 9\n}\n```\n\n**Mark an index as low-priority (best-effort):**\n```json\nPUT /my-archive-index/_settings\n{\n  \"index.routing.allocation.priority\": 1\n}\n```\n\n**Combined with tier routing:**\n```json\nPUT /my-hot-critical-index/_settings\n{\n  \"index.routing.allocation.require._tier\": \"data_hot\",\n  \"index.routing.allocation.priority\": 10\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## 8. Operational Considerations\n\n### 8.1 Backward Compatibility\n\n- The new setting defaults to `1`, so all existing indices behave as before (lowest priority tier) unless explicitly configured.\n- Nodes without `node.attr.allocation.priority` accept all shards, preserving existing behavior.\n- The new allocator is a drop-in replacement; no cluster restart is required.\n\n### 8.2 Priority Inversion Risk\n\nIf all nodes are tagged with `node.attr.allocation.priority: 5` and an index has `index.routing.allocation.priority: 3`, its shards will be unassignable. Operators must ensure that at least some nodes accept each priority level present in the cluster, or leave some nodes untagged as a catch-all.\n\n### 8.3 Rebalancing\n\nThe balance pass (Phase 2 of the allocator) runs without priority filtering. This means that after initial placement, the cluster may rebalance shards across nodes in ways that do not strictly respect priority tiers. This is intentional: long-term balance is more important than strict priority isolation during steady-state operation. Priority ordering is most impactful during cluster recovery and initial shard assignment.\n\n### 8.4 Monitoring\n\nThe following log messages are emitted by `PriorityAllocationDecider` at `TRACE` level:\n- `\"shard [{}] index priority [{}] below node minimum priority [{}], cannot allocate on node [{}]\"`\n- `\"shard [{}] index priority [{}] meets node minimum priority [{}], can allocate on node [{}]\"`\n\nAllocation explain API (`GET /_cluster/allocation/explain`) will surface `PriorityAllocationDecider` decisions under the `\"priority\"` label in the decider breakdown.\n\n### 8.5 Testing Strategy\n\n| Test Class | Coverage |\n|---|---|\n| `PriorityShardsAllocatorTests` | Unit tests for priority-ordered unassigned allocation; verifies high-priority shards consume throttle slots first |\n| `PriorityAllocationDeciderTests` | Unit tests for node attribute matching; YES/NO/THROTTLE decision correctness |\n| `PriorityAllocationIntegrationTests` | Integration tests verifying end-to-end behavior with mixed-priority indices and tagged nodes |\n| `AllocationPriorityTests` (existing) | Unchanged; continues to validate `index.priority` recovery ordering |\n",

This ensures that when node capacity or concurrent\n * recovery slots are limited, higher-priority index shards are placed before lower-priority ones.\n *\n * <p>After priority-ordered initial placement, the standard move and balance passes run\n * without priority filtering to preserve long-term cluster balance.\n *\n * <p>Node-level priority constraints are enforced by the companion\n * {@link PriorityAllocationDecider}, which gates placements based on the\n * {@code node.attr.allocation.priority} node attribute.\n *\n * @see PriorityAllocationDecider\n */\npublic class PriorityShardsAllocator implements ShardsAllocator {\n\n    private static final Logger logger = LogManager.getLogger(PriorityShardsAllocator.class);\n\n    /**\n     * Index-scoped setting that controls the allocation priority tier for an index.\n     *\n     * <p>Valid range: 1 (lowest / default) to 10 (highest). Higher values cause the index's\n     * shards to be allocated before lower-valued indices when node capacity is constrained.\n     * This setting is dynamic and can be changed via the Index Settings API without a restart.\n     *\n     * <p>This setting is distinct from {@link IndexMetadata#INDEX_PRIORITY_SETTING}\n     * ({@code index.priority}), which controls recovery ordering. The two settings are\n     * orthogonal and may be configured independently.\n     */\n    public static final Setting<Integer> INDEX_ROUTING_ALLOCATION_PRIORITY_SETTING = Setting.intSetting(\n        \"index.routing.allocation.priority\",\n        1,   // default: lowest priority tier\n        1,   // minimum\n        10,  // maximum\n        Property.Dynamic,\n        Property.IndexScope\n    );\n\n    private final ShardsAllocator delegate;\n\n    /**\n     * Constructs a {@code PriorityShardsAllocator} wrapping the given delegate allocator.\n     *\n     * @param delegate       the underlying allocator that performs weight-based placement\n     *                       (typically {@link BalancedShardsAllocator})\n     * @param clusterSettings cluster settings, reserved for future cluster-level priority\n     *                        configuration\n     */\n    @Inject\n    public PriorityShardsAllocator(ShardsAllocator delegate, ClusterSettings clusterSettings) {\n        this.delegate = delegate;\n    }\n\n    /**\n     * Allocates shards to nodes using a two-phase strategy:\n     *\n     * <ol>\n     *   <li><b>Priority-ordered unassigned allocation:</b> Unassigned shards are grouped by\n     *       their index's {@link #INDEX_ROUTING_ALLOCATION_PRIORITY_SETTING} and presented to\n     *       the delegate allocator from highest to lowest priority. This ensures throttle slots\n     *       and available node capacity are consumed by high-priority shards first.</li>\n     *   <li><b>Move and balance pass:</b> After all priority groups have been processed, the\n     *       delegate's move and balance logic runs on the full routing table without priority\n     *       filtering, preserving long-term cluster balance.</li>\n     * </ol>\n     *\n     * @param allocation the current routing allocation state, mutated in place\n     */\n    @Override\n    public void allocate(RoutingAllocation allocation) {\n        assert allocation.ignoreDisable() == false;\n\n        if (allocation.routingNodes().size() == 0) {\n            // No data nodes: delegate handles the no-node failure path.\n            delegate.allocate(allocation);\n            return;\n        }\n\n        allocateUnassignedByPriority(allocation);\n\n        // Move and balance passes are priority-agnostic: long-term balance matters more\n        // than priority isolation during steady-state operation.\n        delegate.allocate(allocation);\n    }\n\n    /**\n     * Returns the allocation decision for a single shard, delegating entirely to the underlying\n     * allocator. Priority ordering is a queue-level concern and does not alter per-node decision\n     * logic, so the explain API path is unaffected.\n     *\n     * @param shard      the shard whose allocation decision is requested\n     * @param allocation the current routing allocation state\n     * @return a {@link ShardAllocationDecision} describing where the shard should be placed\n     */\n    @Override\n    public ShardAllocationDecision decideShardAllocation(ShardRouting shard, RoutingAllocation allocation) {\n        return delegate.decideShardAllocation(shard, allocation);\n    }\n\n    /**\n     * Groups all unassigned shards by their index's allocation priority and presents each group\n     * to the delegate allocator in descending priority order (highest first).\n     *\n     * <p>Shards that the delegate cannot place in a given pass remain in the unassigned queue\n     * and are retried in subsequent reroute cycles.\n     *\n     * @param allocation the current routing allocation state\n     */\n    private void allocateUnassignedByPriority(RoutingAllocation allocation) {\n        // TreeMap with reversed order so iteration goes from priority 10 down to 1.\n        Map<Integer, List<ShardRouting>> shardsByPriority = groupUnassignedShardsByPriority(allocation);\n\n        if (shardsByPriority.isEmpty()) {\n            logger.trace(\"no unassigned shards to allocate\");\n            return;\n        }\n\n        logger.debug(\"allocating unassigned shards across {} priority tiers\", shardsByPriority.size());\n\n        for (Map.Entry<Integer, List<ShardRouting>> entry : shardsByPriority.entrySet()) {\n            int priority = entry.getKey();\n            List<ShardRouting> tierShards = entry.getValue();\n            logger.debug(\"allocating {} unassigned shard(s) at priority tier {}\", tierShards.size(), priority);\n\n            /*\n             * TODO: Inject only this tier's shards into the unassigned queue and invoke\n             *       delegate.allocateUnassigned(allocation). The BalancedShardsAllocator's\n             *       Balancer.allocateUnassigned() iterates RoutingNodes.UnassignedShards,\n             *       so the injection mechanism must temporarily replace or filter that\n             *       iterator. One approach is a PriorityFilteredRoutingAllocation wrapper\n             *       that overrides routingNodes().unassigned() to expose only the current\n             *       tier's shards. See design_doc.md \u00a74.2 for the full algorithm.\n             */\n            allocateTier(allocation, tierShards, priority);\n        }\n    }\n\n    /**\n     * Collects all unassigned shards from the routing table and groups them by their index's\n     * {@link #INDEX_ROUTING_ALLOCATION_PRIORITY_SETTING} value.\n     *\n     * @param allocation the current routing allocation state\n     * @return a {@link TreeMap} keyed by priority (descending), each value being the list of\n     *         unassigned shards at that priority tier\n     */\n    private Map<Integer, List<ShardRouting>> groupUnassignedShardsByPriority(RoutingAllocation allocation) {\n        // Reversed comparator: higher priority integers sort first.\n        Map<Integer, List<ShardRouting>> result = new TreeMap<>(Comparator.reverseOrder());\n\n        RoutingNodes.UnassignedShards unassigned = allocation.routingNodes().unassigned();\n        for (ShardRouting shard : unassigned) {\n            IndexMetadata indexMetadata = allocation.metadata().getIndexSafe(shard.index());\n            int priority = INDEX_ROUTING_ALLOCATION_PRIORITY_SETTING.get(indexMetadata.getSettings());\n            result.computeIfAbsent(priority, k -> new ArrayList<>()).add(shard);\n        }\n\n        return result;\n    }\n\n    /**\n     * Allocates a single priority tier's unassigned shards using the delegate allocator.\n     *\n     * <p>This is a placeholder for the tier-scoped allocation invocation. The full\n     * implementation requires a mechanism to expose only {@code tierShards} through the\n     * {@link RoutingNodes.UnassignedShards} iterator seen by the delegate.\n     *\n     * @param allocation the current routing allocation state\n     * @param tierShards the unassigned shards belonging to this priority tier\n     * @param priority   the priority value of this tier (for logging)\n     */\n    private void allocateTier(RoutingAllocation allocation, List<ShardRouting> tierShards, int priority) {\n        // TODO: Implement tier-scoped allocation. Options:\n        //   1. PriorityFilteredRoutingAllocation \u2014 wraps RoutingAllocation and overrides\n        //      routingNodes().unassigned() to return only tierShards.\n        //   2. Direct manipulation of the UnassignedShards queue with save/restore of\n        //      non-tier shards (requires RoutingNodes API extension).\n        //   3. Invoke BalancedShardsAllocator.Balancer.allocateUnassigned() directly via\n        //      a package-private hook (requires moving PriorityShardsAllocator into the\n        //      same package or using a friend accessor pattern).\n        logger.trace(\"allocating tier {} ({} shards) \u2014 implementation pending\", priority, tierShards.size());\n    }\n\n    // -------------------------------------------------------------------------\n    // Inner class: PriorityAllocationDecider\n    // -------------------------------------------------------------------------\n\n    /**\n     * An {@link AllocationDecider} that enforces node-level allocation priority constraints.\n     *\n     * <p>Nodes may be tagged with the {@code node.attr.allocation.priority} attribute to\n     * designate them as dedicated hosts for high-priority indices. A node tagged with value\n     * {@code N} will only accept shards from indices whose\n     * {@link #INDEX_ROUTING_ALLOCATION_PRIORITY_SETTING} is {@code >= N}.\n     *\n     * <p>Nodes without the attribute are unrestricted and accept shards from any index.\n     *\n     * <h3>Example</h3>\n     * <pre>\n     * # elasticsearch.yml \u2014 reserve this node for priority-7-and-above indices\n     * node.attr.allocation.priority: 7\n     * </pre>\n     *\n     * <pre>\n     * # Index settings \u2014 mark index as priority 9 (accepted by the node above)\n     * PUT /my-critical-index/_settings\n     * { \"index.routing.allocation.priority\": 9 }\n     * </pre>\n     *\n     * <h3>canRemain behavior</h3>\n     * If a node's {@code node.attr.allocation.priority} is raised (e.g., via rolling restart),\n     * shards from indices whose priority falls below the new threshold receive a {@code NO}\n     * from {@link #canRemain}, triggering relocation to nodes that accept them.\n     */\n    public static class PriorityAllocationDecider extends AllocationDecider {\n\n        /** Decider label used in allocation explain API responses. */\n        public static final String NAME = \"priority\";\n\n        /**\n         * Node attribute key that specifies the minimum index allocation priority this node\n         * will accept. Absent means the node is unrestricted.\n         */\n        static final String NODE_ATTR_ALLOCATION_PRIORITY = \"allocation.priority\";\n\n        /**\n         * Returns a {@link Decision} on whether the given shard can be allocated to the given\n         * node based on priority constraints.\n         *\n         * <ul>\n         *   <li>If the node has no {@code node.attr.allocation.priority} attribute, returns\n         *       {@link Decision#YES} (unrestricted node).</li>\n         *   <li>If the index's priority meets or exceeds the node's minimum, returns\n         *       {@link Decision#YES}.</li>\n         *   <li>Otherwise returns {@link Decision#NO} with an explanation.</li>\n         * </ul>\n         *\n         * @param shardRouting the shard being considered for allocation\n         * @param node         the candidate target node\n         * @param allocation   the current routing allocation state\n         * @return the allocation decision\n         */\n        @Override\n        public Decision canAllocate(ShardRouting shardRouting, RoutingNode node, RoutingAllocation allocation) {\n            return decidePriority(shardRouting, node, allocation);\n        }\n\n        /**\n         * Returns a {@link Decision} on whether the given shard can remain on the given node.\n         * Uses the same priority-matching logic as {@link #canAllocate}.\n         *\n         * @param indexMetadata metadata for the shard's index\n         * @param shardRouting  the shard being evaluated\n         * @param node          the node currently hosting the shard\n         * @param allocation    the current routing allocation state\n         * @return the allocation decision\n         */\n        @Override\n        public Decision canRemain(\n            IndexMetadata indexMetadata,\n            ShardRouting shardRouting,\n            RoutingNode node,\n            RoutingAllocation allocation\n        ) {\n            return decidePriority(shardRouting, node, allocation);\n        }\n\n        /**\n         * Core priority-matching logic shared by {@link #canAllocate} and {@link #canRemain}.\n         *\n         * @param shardRouting the shard being evaluated\n         * @param node         the candidate or current node\n         * @param allocation   the current routing allocation state\n         * @return {@link Decision#YES} if the placement is allowed, {@link Decision#NO} otherwise\n         */\n        private Decision decidePriority(ShardRouting shardRouting, RoutingNode node, RoutingAllocation allocation) {\n            String nodeAttrValue = node.node().getAttributes().get(NODE_ATTR_ALLOCATION_PRIORITY);\n\n            if (nodeAttrValue == null) {\n                // Node has no priority restriction \u2014 accept any index.\n                return allocation.decision(\n                    Decision.YES,\n                    NAME,\n                    \"node [%s] has no allocation priority restriction\",\n                    node.nodeId()\n                );\n            }\n\n            int nodeMinPriority;\n            try {\n                nodeMinPriority = Integer.parseInt(nodeAttrValue);\n            } catch (NumberFormatException e) {\n                // Misconfigured attribute \u2014 fail open with a warning rather than blocking allocation.\n                logger.warn(\n                    \"node [{}] has non-integer value [{}] for attribute [{}]; ignoring priority constraint\",\n                    node.nodeId(),\n                    nodeAttrValue,\n                    NODE_ATTR_ALLOCATION_PRIORITY\n                );\n                return allocation.decision(\n                    Decision.YES,\n                    NAME,\n                    \"node [%s] attribute [%s] value [%s] is not a valid integer; constraint ignored\",\n                    node.nodeId(),\n                    NODE_ATTR_ALLOCATION_PRIORITY,\n                    nodeAttrValue\n                );\n            }\n\n            IndexMetadata indexMetadata = allocation.metadata().getIndexSafe(shardRouting.index());\n            int indexPriority = INDEX_ROUTING_ALLOCATION_PRIORITY_SETTING.get(indexMetadata.getSettings());\n\n            if (indexPriority >= nodeMinPriority) {\n                logger.trace(\n                    \"shard [{}] index priority [{}] meets node [{}] minimum priority [{}]\",\n                    shardRouting.shardId(),\n                    indexPriority,\n                    node.nodeId(),\n                    nodeMinPriority\n                );\n                return allocation.decision(\n                    Decision.YES,\n                    NAME,\n                    \"index priority [%d] meets node [%s] minimum allocation priority [%d]\",\n                    indexPriority,\n                    node.nodeId(),\n                    nodeMinPriority\n                );\n            }\n\n            logger.trace(\n                \"shard [{}] index priority [{}] below node [{}] minimum priority [{}]; cannot allocate\",\n                shardRouting.shardId(),\n                indexPriority,\n                node.nodeId(),\n                nodeMinPriority\n            );\n            return allocation.decision(\n                Decision.NO,\n                NAME,\n indexPriority,\n                node.nodeId(),\n                nodeMinPriority,\n                INDEX_ROUTING_ALLOCATION_PRIORITY_SETTING.getKey(),\n                nodeMinPriority,\n                NODE_ATTR_ALLOCATION_PRIORITY\n            );\n        }\n    }\n}\n",

These are independent constraints in the same namespace; both must pass for a placement to proceed.\n311:`ThrottlingAllocationDecider` limits concurrent recoveries per node. Because `PriorityShardsAllocator` presents high-priority shards first, throttle slots are consumed by high-priority shards before low-priority ones even get to the throttle check. This is the primary mechanism by which priority ordering translates into preferential resource consumption.\n315:Disk constraints are absolute and take precedence over priority. A high-priority shard cannot be placed on a node that has exceeded the high watermark. The priority ordering in `PriorityShardsAllocator` ensures that when disk space is available, it is allocated to high-priority shards first.\n327:If `DesiredBalanceShardsAllocator` is the active allocator (the default in recent Elasticsearch versions), `PriorityShardsAllocator` wraps it as the delegate instead of `BalancedShardsAllocator` directly. The desired-balance computation loop in `DesiredBalanceComputer` would need to be made priority-aware by sorting its internal unassigned shard iteration. PriorityFilteredRoutingAllocation \u2014 wraps RoutingAllocation and overrides\n   211\t        //      routingNodes().unassigned() to return only tierShards.\n   212\t        //   2.
